## 1. Fix Watsonx Integration
**Files:** `traincli/llm.py`, `.env.example`

**What's broken:**
- Current `llm.py` is written for Groq
- Watsonx SDK call is failing with credentials error
- Model name needs to change to Granite instruct

**Exact changes needed:**

Replace the entire `_call()` function in `llm.py` with watsonx SDK:

```python
from ibm_watsonx_ai import APIClient, Credentials
from ibm_watsonx_ai.foundation_models import ModelInference

def _get_model():
    credentials = Credentials(
        url=os.getenv("WATSONX_URL", "https://us-south.ml.cloud.ibm.com"),
        api_key=os.getenv("WATSONX_API_KEY")
    )
    client = APIClient(credentials, project_id=os.getenv("WATSONX_PROJECT_ID"))
    return ModelInference(
        model_id=os.getenv("LLM_MODEL", "ibm/granite-13b-instruct-v2"),
        api_client=client,
        params={"max_new_tokens": 800, "temperature": 0.2}
    )
```

**What needs to be available:**
- `WATSONX_API_KEY` — IBM Cloud API key
- `WATSONX_PROJECT_ID` — from watsonx.ai dashboard
- `WATSONX_URL` — region URL
- `pip install ibm-watsonx-ai` added to dependencies

**Definition of done:** Running `train --data data.csv --target col --auto` shows interpretation text generated by Granite, not the fallback static text.

---

## 2. Fix Data Leakage Detection
**Files:** `traincli/profiler.py`, `traincli/cleaner.py`

**What's broken:**
- DS Jobs dataset got R²=1.0 because `min_salary` and `max_salary` are mathematically derived from `avg_salary`
- TrainCLI didn't catch or warn about this
- Users will think their model is perfect when it's actually cheating

**Exact changes needed:**

In `profiler.py` add a leakage detector function:

```python
def detect_leakage(df: pd.DataFrame, target: str) -> list:
    leakage_suspects = []
    target_series = df[target]
    
    for col in df.columns:
        if col == target:
            continue
            
        # Check 1: correlation too perfect
        if pd.api.types.is_numeric_dtype(df[col]):
            corr = abs(df[col].corr(target_series))
            if corr > 0.98:
                leakage_suspects.append({
                    "col": col,
                    "reason": f"correlation with target is {corr:.3f} — suspiciously high",
                    "severity": "high"
                })
        
        # Check 2: column name contains target name
        if target.lower() in col.lower() and col != target:
            leakage_suspects.append({
                "col": col,
                "reason": f"column name contains target name '{target}'",
                "severity": "high"
            })
        
        # Check 3: linear combination check
        # if col = target * constant, it's leakage
        if pd.api.types.is_numeric_dtype(df[col]) and pd.api.types.is_numeric_dtype(target_series):
            try:
                ratio = (target_series / df[col].replace(0, float('nan'))).dropna()
                if ratio.std() < 0.01:
                    leakage_suspects.append({
                        "col": col,
                        "reason": f"appears to be a linear transformation of target",
                        "severity": "high"
                    })
            except Exception:
                pass
    
    return leakage_suspects
```

In `cli.py` add a `--drop` flag:

```python
@click.option("--drop", default=None, 
    help="Comma-separated columns to drop e.g. --drop col1,col2")
```

And process it before training:

```python
if drop:
    cols_to_drop = [c.strip() for c in drop.split(",")]
    df_clean = df_clean.drop(columns=cols_to_drop, errors="ignore")
```

**Definition of done:** Running on DS Jobs without `--drop` prints:

```
⚠ Leakage suspected:
  → min_salary: correlation with target is 0.999 — suspiciously high
  → max_salary: column name contains target name 'salary'
  
  Suggested fix: train --drop min_salary,max_salary ...
```

## 3. Build the Meta-model
**New files:** `traincli/meta_collector.py`, `traincli/meta_model.pkl`, script `scripts/build_meta.py`

**What needs to happen in order:**

**3a. Add `--meta` flag to CLI**

After every successful run, append one row to `~/.traincli/meta_dataset.csv`:

```python
{
    "rows": 660,
    "cols": 26,
    "null_pct": 0.0,
    "numeric_ratio": 0.73,
    "categorical_ratio": 0.27,
    "target_nunique": 25,
    "target_is_float": 0,
    "target_range": 228,
    "best_model": "gradient_boosting",  # whichever won CV
    "best_cv_score": 0.798,
}
```

**3b. Collect data**

Run TrainCLI with `--meta` flag on as many public datasets as possible. Minimum viable: 40-50 runs. These are easy to get:

```bash
# sklearn built-ins
python scripts/fetch_sklearn_datasets.py
# fetches: iris, wine, breast_cancer, diabetes, digits
# runs traincli on each, appends to meta_dataset.csv
```

**3c. Train the meta-model**

```bash
train --data ~/.traincli/meta_dataset.csv --target best_model --auto
```

Copy the output `model.pkl` to `traincli/meta_model.pkl`

**3d. Use it in trainer.py**

In `_auto_select()`, check meta-model first:

```python
meta_rec = _meta_predict(X, problem_type)
if meta_rec:
    info(f"Meta-model recommends: [bold]{meta_rec}[/bold]")
    # still run CV to confirm
    # if CV agrees → high confidence
    # if CV disagrees → trust CV but note it
```

**Definition of done:** Running `train --data data.csv --target col` prints:

```
→ Meta-model recommends: Gradient Boosting
→ CV confirmed: Gradient Boosting ✓
```

## 4. Build the MCP Server
**New file:** `traincli/mcp_server.py`

**What needs to happen:**

**4a. Install MCP SDK**

```bash
pip install mcp
```

Add to `pyproject.toml` dependencies.

**4b. Refactor CLI into a core function**

Right now all logic is inside `_run_single()` in `cli.py`. The MCP server needs to call the same pipeline. Extract it into `traincli/core.py`:

```python
# traincli/core.py
def run_pipeline(data_path, target, model_key=None, 
                 task=None, out="./output", auto=True) -> dict:
    """Core pipeline — called by both CLI and MCP server"""
    # move all logic from _run_single() here
    # return results dict
```

Then `cli.py` just calls `core.run_pipeline()` and MCP server does the same.

**4c. Write the MCP server**

Three tools exposed:

```python
@server.tool()
async def train_model(data: str, target: str, auto: bool = True) -> dict:
    """Train an ML model on a CSV file"""

@server.tool()  
async def profile_dataset(data: str) -> dict:
    """Profile a CSV and return insights about it"""

@server.tool()
async def suggest_target(data: str) -> dict:
    """Suggest the best target column for a dataset"""
```

**4d. Add entry point to pyproject.toml**

```toml
[project.scripts]
train = "traincli.cli:main"
traincli-mcp = "traincli.mcp_server:main"
```

**4e. Add MCP config instructions to README**

```json
{
  "mcpServers": {
    "traincli": {
      "command": "traincli-mcp"
    }
  }
}
```

**Definition of done:** Claude Code can call `train_model` tool and get back metrics without user opening a terminal.

## 5. Add `train init` Command
**Files:** `traincli/cli.py`, new `traincli/config.py`

**What it does:**

```bash
$ train init

TrainCLI Setup
──────────────
LLM Provider [watsonx/groq/none]: watsonx
WatsonX API Key: ****
WatsonX Project ID: ****
WatsonX URL [https://us-south.ml.cloud.ibm.com]: 

✓ Config saved to C:\Users\Dennis\.traincli\config.env
✓ Run: train --data ./data.csv --target column
```

Saves to `~/.traincli/config.env` — global, works from any directory.

`llm.py` load order:

```python
# 1. Environment variables
# 2. ~/.traincli/config.env  ← train init writes here
# 3. .env in current dir     ← developer mode
# 4. No key → offline mode
```

**Definition of done:** Fresh `pip install traincli` user runs `train init`, enters keys once, never touches a `.env` file again.

---

## 6. Fix the Usage Block in Generated train.py
**File:** `traincli/exporter.py`

**What's broken:**
- Usage block includes columns that don't exist after cleaning
- Doesn't filter to only the features the model actually trained on
- Missing encoding step causes the `ValueError` you hit earlier

**Exact fix:**

In `_build_train_py()`, the usage block should only include `results["feature_names"]` — which is already the post-cleaning, post-encoding feature list. Make sure encoding is always shown:

```python
# ── HOW TO USE ──
# import pickle, pandas as pd
# from sklearn.preprocessing import LabelEncoder
# 
# with open("model.pkl", "rb") as f:
#     model = pickle.load(f)
#
# new_data = pd.DataFrame([{
#     "Rating": ...,          # numeric
#     "Size": ...,            # categorical — will be encoded
#     "python": ...,          # numeric (0 or 1)
# }])
#
# # Required: encode categoricals the same way as training
# for col in new_data.select_dtypes(include="object").columns:
#     le = LabelEncoder()
#     new_data[col] = le.fit_transform(new_data[col].astype(str))
#
# print(model.predict(new_data))
```

Also add dtype hints as comments next to each feature so user knows what type to pass.

**Definition of done:** Running the generated `train.py` usage example works out of the box with no errors.

228 | df = pd.read_csv("{data_path}")
229 | 
230 | 
231 | # ── 2. CLEANING ──────────────────────────────────────────────
232 | # Changes made during TrainCLI run — replicate for new data:
233 | {cleaning_block}
234 | 
235 | 
236 | # ── 3. FEATURES & TARGET ─────────────────────────────────────
237 | X = df.drop(columns=["{target}"])
238 | y = df["{target}"]
239 | 
240 | # Encode categorical string columns to numeric
241 | for col in X.select_dtypes(include="object").columns:
242 |     le = LabelEncoder()
243 |     X[col] = le.fit_transform(X[col].astype(str))
244 | 
245 | {"# Encode target (categorical detected)" + chr(10) + "le_target = LabelEncoder()" + chr(10) + "y = pd.Series(le_target.fit_transform(y))" if problem_type == "classification" else "# Target is numeric — no encoding needed"}
246 | 
247 | 
248 | # ── 4. TRAIN / TEST SPLIT ────────────────────────────────────
249 | # 80/20 split, stratified to preserve class balance
250 | X_train, X_test, y_train, y_test = train_test_split(
251 |     X, y,
252 |     test_size=0.2,
253 |     random_state=42,
254 |     {stratify_line}
255 | )
256 | 
257 | 
258 | # ── 5. PIPELINE ──────────────────────────────────────────────
259 | # {preproc_comment}
260 | pipeline = Pipeline([
261 |     ("imputer", SimpleImputer(strategy="median")),
262 |     ("scaler",  StandardScaler()),
263 | 
264 |     # {model_comment}
265 |     {source_comment}
266 |     ("model", {class_name}({params_str})),
267 | ])
268 | 
269 | 
270 | # ── 6. CROSS VALIDATION ──────────────────────────────────────
271 | # 3-fold CV checks stability before committing to full fit
272 | cv_scores = cross_val_score(pipeline, X_train, y_train, cv=3)
273 | print(f"CV Score: {{cv_scores.mean():.3f}} ± {{cv_scores.std():.3f}}")
274 | 
275 | 
276 | # ── 7. TRAIN ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
277 | pipeline.fit(X_train, y_train)
278 | 
279 | 
280 | # ── 8. EVALUATE ──────────────────────────────────────────────
281 | # {results_comment}
282 | y_pred = pipeline.predict(X_test)
283 | print("\\n── Evaluation ──────────────────────────")
284 | {eval_line}
285 | 
286 | 
287 | # ── 9. CONFIDENCE NOTE ───────────────────────────────────────
288 | # Confidence: {confidence}
289 | {conf_lines}
290 | 
291 | 
292 | # ── 10. SAVE MODEL ───────────────────────────────────────────
293 | with open("model.pkl", "wb") as f:
294 |     pickle.dump(pipeline, f)
295 | print("\\n✓ Model saved to model.pkl")

<file><path>traincli/profiler.py</path>
<content lines="1-142">
  1 | import pandas as pd
  2 | import numpy as np
  3 | from traincli.utils.display import header, info, warn, profile_table
  4 | 
  5 | 
  6 | def profile(df: pd.DataFrame, target: str) -> dict:
  7 |     """
  8 |     Analyze a dataframe and return a structured profile.
  9 |     No LLM involved — pure pandas.
 10 |     """
 11 |     header("Profiling dataset")
 12 | 
 13 |     rows, cols = df.shape
 14 |     null_count = int(df.isnull().sum().sum())
 15 |     null_pct = (null_count / (rows * cols)) * 100
 16 | 
 17 |     col_profiles = {}
 18 |     issues = []
 19 | 
 20 |     for col in df.columns:
 21 |         series = df[col]
 22 |         col_info = {
 23 |             "dtype": str(series.dtype),
 24 |             "null_count": int(series.isnull().sum()),
 25 |             "null_pct": round(series.isnull().sum() / len(series) * 100, 2),
 26 |             "nunique": int(series.nunique()),
 27 |             "is_target": col == target,
 28 |         }
 29 | 
 30 |         # Numeric columns
 31 |         if pd.api.types.is_numeric_dtype(series):
 32 |             col_info["type"] = "numeric"
 33 |             col_info["min"] = float(series.min()) if not series.isnull().all() else None
 34 |             col_info["max"] = float(series.max()) if not series.isnull().all() else None
 35 |             col_info["mean"] = float(series.mean()) if not series.isnull().all() else None
 36 | 
 37 |             # Detect impossible values by column name heuristics
 38 |             if col.lower() in ["age", "years"] and col_info["min"] is not None:
 39 |                 if col_info["min"] < 0 or col_info["max"] > 150:
 40 |                     issues.append({
 41 |                         "col": col,
 42 |                         "type": "impossible_values",
 43 |                         "detail": f"values outside plausible range ({col_info['min']} to {col_info['max']})",
 44 |                         "auto_fixable": False,
 45 |                     })
 46 | 
 47 |         # Object columns — check for mixed numeric/text
 48 |         elif series.dtype == object:
 49 |             numeric_parseable = pd.to_numeric(series.dropna(), errors="coerce").notna().sum()
 50 |             total_non_null = series.dropna().shape[0]
 51 | 
 52 |             if total_non_null > 0:
 53 |                 numeric_ratio = numeric_parseable / total_non_null
 54 |                 if 0.5 < numeric_ratio < 1.0:
 55 |                     col_info["type"] = "mixed_numeric"
 56 |                     issues.append({
 57 |                         "col": col,
 58 |                         "type": "mixed_type",
 59 |                         "detail": f"{int((1 - numeric_ratio) * total_non_null)} non-numeric values in what looks like a numeric column",
 60 |                         "auto_fixable": False,
 61 |                     })
 62 |                 elif col_info["nunique"] == rows:
 63 |                     col_info["type"] = "id_like"
 64 |                     issues.append({
 65 |                         "col": col,
 66 |                         "type": "id_column",
 67 |                         "detail": "unique per row — likely an ID, not a feature",
 68 |                         "auto_fixable": True,
 69 |                     })
 70 |                 elif col_info["nunique"] <= 2 and col == target:
 71 |                     col_info["type"] = "binary_target"
 72 |                 else:
 73 |                     col_info["type"] = "categorical"
 74 | 
 75 |         # Datetime columns
 76 |         elif pd.api.types.is_datetime64_any_dtype(series):
 77 |             col_info["type"] = "datetime"
 78 | 
 79 |         # Check for date-like strings
 80 |         if series.dtype == object and col.lower() in ["date", "created_at", "updated_at", "joined", "date_joined", "timestamp"]:
 81 |             col_info["likely_date"] = True
 82 |             issues.append({
 83 |                 "col": col,
 84 |                 "type": "date_string",
 85 |                 "detail": "looks like a date column stored as text",
 86 |                 "auto_fixable": True,
 87 |             })
 88 | 
 89 |         # High null warning
 90 |         if col_info["null_pct"] > 40 and col != target:
 91 |             issues.append({
 92 |                 "col": col,
 93 |                 "type": "high_nulls",
 94 |                 "detail": f"{col_info['null_pct']:.0f}% missing values",
 95 |                 "auto_fixable": False,
 96 |             })
 97 | 
 98 |         # Mixed target encoding (yes/no/1/0/True)
 99 |         if col == target and series.dtype == object:
100 |             unique_vals = set(series.dropna().str.lower().unique())
101 |             bool_variants = {"yes", "no", "true", "false", "1", "0", "y", "n"}
102 |             if unique_vals.issubset(bool_variants):
103 |                 issues.append({
104 |                     "col": col,
105 |                     "type": "mixed_target_encoding",
106 |                     "detail": f"target has mixed encodings: {list(series.unique()[:5])}",
107 |                     "auto_fixable": True,
108 |                 })
109 | 
110 |         col_profiles[col] = col_info
111 | 
112 |     # Free text detection (high avg string length, object dtype, not target)
113 |     for col in df.select_dtypes(include="object").columns:
114 |         if col == target:
115 |             continue
116 |         avg_len = df[col].dropna().astype(str).str.len().mean()
117 |         if avg_len > 50:
118 |             issues.append({
119 |                 "col": col,
120 |                 "type": "free_text",
121 |                 "detail": f"looks like free text (avg {avg_len:.0f} chars) — low signal for tabular ML",
122 |                 "auto_fixable": True,
123 |             })
124 | 
125 |     result = {
126 |         "rows": rows,
127 |         "cols": cols,
128 |         "target": target,
129 |         "null_count": null_count,
130 |         "null_pct": round(null_pct, 2),
131 |         "columns": col_profiles,
132 |         "issues": issues,
133 |     }
134 | 
135 |     profile_table(result)
136 | 
137 |     if issues:
138 |         warn(f"Found {len(issues)} issue(s) in your dataset")
139 |     else:
140 |         info("No obvious issues detected")
141 | 
142 |     return result
</content>
</file>

  1 | import click
  2 | import pandas as pd
  3 | from pathlib import Path
  4 | from rich.console import Console
  5 | 
  6 | from traincli.utils.display import banner, header, success, warn, error, info, blank
  7 | from traincli.utils.session import Session
  8 | from traincli.profiler import profile
  9 | from traincli.cleaner import clean
 10 | from traincli.detector import detect
 11 | from traincli.trainer import train, improve
 12 | from traincli.exporter import export
 13 | 
 14 | console = Console()
 15 | 
 16 | 
 17 | @click.command()
 18 | @click.option("--data",    "-d", default=None, help="Path to CSV file")
 19 | @click.option("--dir",     "-D", "data_dir", default=None, help="Directory of CSV files")
 20 | @click.option("--target",  "-t", required=True, help="Target column name")
 21 | @click.option("--model",   "-m", default=None, help="Model key, or '?' to pick interactively")
 22 | @click.option("--task",          default=None, type=click.Choice(["classification", "regression"]), help="Override problem type detection")
 23 | @click.option("--improve",       "improve_model", default=None, help="Path to existing model.pkl to retrain")
 24 | @click.option("--out",     "-o", default="./output", help="Output directory (default: ./output)")
 25 | @click.option("--preview",       is_flag=True, help="Preview without training")
 26 | @click.option("--auto",          is_flag=True, help="Skip interactive prompts")
 27 | def main(data, data_dir, target, model, task, improve_model, out, preview, auto):
 28 |     """
 29 |     TrainCLI — train ML models from a single command.
 30 | 
 31 |     \b
 32 |     Examples:
 33 |       train --data ./sales.csv --target churn
 34 |       train --data ./sales.csv --target price --model random_forest
 35 |       train --data ./sales.csv --target price --model ?
 36 |       train --data ./sales.csv --target churn --task classification
 37 |       train --improve ./output/model.pkl --data ./new_data.csv --target churn

 64 |

 76 | def _run_single(data_path, target, model_key, task, out, preview, auto):
 77 |     path = Path(data_path)
 78 |     if not path.exists():
 79 |         error(f"File not found: {data_path}")
 80 |         raise click.Abort()
 81 | 
 82 |     # Load
 83 |     header("Loading dataset")
 84 |     try:
 85 |         df = pd.read_csv(path)
 86 |     except Exception as e:
 87 |         error(f"Could not read CSV: {e}")
 88 |         raise click.Abort()
 89 | 
 90 |     if target not in df.columns:
 91 |         error(f"Target '{target}' not found. Available: {list(df.columns)}")
 92 |         raise click.Abort()
 93 | 
 94 |     info(f"Loaded {len(df):,} rows × {len(df.columns)} columns from {path.name}")
 95 | 
 96 |     session = Session(data_path, target)
 97 | 
 98 |     # Profile
 99 |     prof = profile(df, target)
100 |     session.set_profile({
101 |         "rows": prof["rows"],
102 |         "cols": prof["cols"],
103 |         "null_pct": prof["null_pct"],
104 |         "issues_found": len(prof["issues"]),
105 |     })
106 | 
107 |     # Preview
108 |     if preview:
109 |         blank()
110 |         _print_preview(df, prof, target, model_key)
111 |         return
112 | 
113 |     # Clean
114 |     df_clean = clean(df, prof, session, auto=auto)
115 | 
116 |     # Detect problem type
117 |     if task:
118 |         # User override
119 |         from traincli.utils.display import success as disp_success
120 |         disp_success(f"Problem type: [bold]{task}[/bold]  [dim](manually specified)[/dim]")
121 |         session.set_problem(task, "user_flag")
122 |         problem_type = task
123 |     else:
124 |         problem_type = detect(df_clean, target, session)
125 | 
126 |     # Train
127 |     results = train(
128 |         df=df_clean,
129 |         target=target,
130 |         problem_type=problem_type,
131 |         session=session,
132 |         model_key=model_key,
133 |         interactive=not auto,
134 |         profile=prof,
135 |     )
136 | 
137 |     # Export
138 |     output_dir = Path(out)
139 |     export(results, df_clean, target, data_path, output_dir, session)
140 | 
141 |     blank()
142 |     console.print("[bold green]Done![/bold green]")
143 |     console.print(f"  Output : [cyan]{output_dir.resolve()}[/cyan]")
144 |     console.print(f"  Files  : model.pkl · train.py · report.md · metrics.json · session.json")
145 |     blank()
146 |

148 | def _run_folder(data_dir, target, model_key, task, out, auto):
149 |     from rich.table import Table
150 |     from rich import box
151 | 
152 |     folder = Path(data_dir)
153 |     if not folder.exists() or not folder.is_dir():
154 |         error(f"Directory not found: {data_dir}")
155 |         raise click.Abort()
156 | 
157 |     csv_files = list(folder.glob("*.csv"))
158 |     if not csv_files:
159 |         error(f"No CSV files found in {data_dir}")
160 |         raise click.Abort()
161 | 
162 |     info(f"Found {len(csv_files)} CSV file(s)")
163 |     blank()
164 | 
165 |     summary_rows = []
166 |     output_base = Path(out)
167 | 
168 |     for csv_path in csv_files:
169 |         console.rule(f"[cyan]{csv_path.name}[/cyan]")
170 |         sub_out = output_base / csv_path.stem
171 | 
172 |         try:
173 |             df = pd.read_csv(csv_path)
174 |             if target not in df.columns:
175 |                 warn(f"Target '{target}' not found in {csv_path.name} — skipping")
176 |                 summary_rows.append({"file": csv_path.name, "status": "skipped", "model": "-", "score": "-", "confidence": "-"})
177 |                 continue
178 | 
179 |             session = Session(str(csv_path), target)
180 |             prof = profile(df, target)
181 |             session.set_profile({"rows": prof["rows"], "cols": prof["cols"], "null_pct": prof["null_pct"], "issues_found": len(prof["issues"])})
182 |             df_clean = clean(df, prof, session, auto=True)
183 | 
184 |             if task:
185 |                 problem_type = task
186 |                 session.set_problem(task, "user_flag")
187 |             else:
188 |                 problem_type = detect(df_clean, target, session)
189 | 
190 |             results = train(df_clean, target, problem_type, session, model_key=model_key, interactive=False, profile=prof)
191 |             export(results, df_clean, target, str(csv_path), sub_out, session)
192 | 
193 |             primary = list(results["metrics"].values())[0]
194 |             summary_rows.append({
195 |                 "file": csv_path.name,
196 |                 "status": "done",
197 |                 "model": results["model_entry"]["label"],
198 |                 "score": primary,
199 |                 "confidence": results["confidence"],
200 |             })
201 | 
202 |         except Exception as e:
203 |             error(f"Failed on {csv_path.name}: {e}")
204 |             summary_rows.append({"file": csv_path.name, "status": "error", "model": "-", "score": "-", "confidence": "-"})
205 | 
206 |     # Summary table
207 |     blank()
208 |     console.rule("[bold]Summary[/bold]")
209 |     blank()
210 |     table = Table(box=box.SIMPLE, show_header=True, header_style="bold")
211 |     table.add_column("File")
212 |     table.add_column("Status")
213 |     table.add_column("Model")
214 |     table.add_column("Score")
215 |     table.add_column("Confidence")
216 | 
217 |     for row in summary_rows:
218 |         s = row["status"]
219 |         color = "green" if s == "done" else "red" if s == "error" else "yellow"
220 |         table.add_row(row["file"], f"[{color}]{s}[/{color}]", row["model"], row["score"], row["confidence"])
221 | 
222 |     console.print(table)
223 |     _write_folder_summary(summary_rows, output_base, target)
224 |     success(f"summary.md → {output_base / 'summary.md'}")
225 |     blank()
226 | 
227 | 
228 | def _print_preview(df, prof, target, model_key):
229 |     console.print("[bold]Preview mode — nothing will be trained[/bold]")
230 |     blank()
231 |     console.print(f"  Dataset : {prof['rows']:,} rows × {prof['cols']} columns")
232 |     console.print(f"  Target  : {target}")
233 |     auto   = sum(1 for i in prof["issues"] if i["auto_fixable"])
234 |     manual = len(prof["issues"]) - auto
235 |     console.print(f"  Issues  : {len(prof['issues'])} found ({auto} auto-fix, {manual} need input)")
236 |     console.print(f"  Model   : {'auto-select via CV' if not model_key or model_key == '?' else model_key}")
237 |     blank()
238 |     console.print("Run without [cyan]--preview[/cyan] to train.")
239 | 
240 | 
241 | def _write_folder_summary(rows, output_dir, target):
242 |     output_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
243 |     lines = [
244 |         "# TrainCLI — Folder Run Summary",
245 |         "",
246 |         f"**Target:** `{target}`  ",
247 |         f"**Generated:** {pd.Timestamp.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M')}",
248 |         "",
249 |         "| File | Status | Model | Score | Confidence |",
250 |         "|------|--------|-------|-------|------------|",
251 |     ]
252 |     for row in rows:
253 |         lines.append(f"| {row['file']} | {row['status']} | {row['model']} | {row['score']} | {row['confidence']} |")
254 | 
255 |     with open(output_dir / "summary.md", "w") as f:
256 |         f.write("\n".join(lines))
257 | 
258 | 
259 | if __name__ == "__main__":
260 |     main()

import pandas as pd

def profile(df: pd.DataFrame, target: str) -> dict:
=======
import pandas as pd
import numpy as np
from traincli.utils.display import header, info, warn, profile_table


def detect_leakage(df: pd.DataFrame, target: str) -> list:
    """
    Detect potential data leakage — features that are suspiciously correlated
    with the target or derived from it.
    """
    leakage_suspects = []
    target_series = df[target]
    
    for col in df.columns:
        if col == target:
            continue
            
        # Check 1: correlation too perfect
        if pd.api.types.is_numeric_dtype(df[col]) and pd.api.types.is_numeric_dtype(target_series):
            try:
                corr = abs(df[col].corr(target_series))
                if corr > 0.98:
                    leakage_suspects.append({
                        "col": col,
                        "reason": f"correlation with target is {corr:.3f} — suspiciously high",
                        "severity": "high"
                    })
            except Exception:
                pass
        
        # Check 2: column name contains target name
        if target.lower() in col.lower() and col != target:
            leakage_suspects.append({
                "col": col,
                "reason": f"column name contains target name '{target}'",
                "severity": "high"
            })
        
        # Check 3: linear combination check
        # if col = target * constant, it's leakage
        if pd.api.types.is_numeric_dtype(df[col]) and pd.api.types.is_numeric_dtype(target_series):
            try:
                ratio = (target_series / df[col].replace(0, float('nan'))).dropna()
                if len(ratio) > 0 and ratio.std() < 0.01:
                    leakage_suspects.append({
                        "col": col,
                        "reason": f"appears to be a linear transformation of target",
                        "severity": "high"
                    })
            except Exception:
                pass
    
    return leakage_suspects


def profile(df: pd.DataFrame, target: str) -> dict:

    else:

    return result

    # Check for data leakage
    leakage = detect_leakage(df, target)
    
    result = {
        "rows": rows,
        "cols": cols,
        "target": target,
        "null_count": null_count,
        "null_pct": round(null_pct, 2),
        "columns": col_profiles,
        "issues": issues,
        "leakage": leakage,
    }

    profile_table(result)

    if issues:
        warn(f"Found {len(issues)} issue(s) in your dataset")
    else:
        info("No obvious issues detected")
    
    # Display leakage warnings
    if leakage:
        from rich.console import Console
        console = Console()
        console.print("\n[bold yellow]⚠ Leakage suspected:[/bold yellow]")
        for leak in leakage:
            console.print(f"  → [cyan]{leak['col']}[/cyan]: {leak['reason']}")
        
        # Suggest fix
        cols_to_drop = ",".join([l["col"] for l in leakage])
        console.print(f"\n  [dim]Suggested fix:[/dim] train --drop {cols_to_drop} ...\n")

    return result

        cols_to_drop = [c.strip() for c in drop.split(",")]
        cols_to_drop = [c for c in cols_to_drop if c in df.columns and c != target]
        if cols_to_drop:
            info(f"Dropping columns: {', '.join(cols_to_drop)}")
            df = df.drop(columns=cols_to_drop)
    
    # Clean
    df_clean = clean(df, prof, session, auto=auto)

 18 | def _available() -> bool:
 19 |     """Check if LLM credentials are available."""
 20 |     if LLM_PROVIDER == "watsonx":
 21 |         return bool(WATSONX_API_KEY and WATSONX_PROJECT_ID)
 22 |     return False

 24 | 
 25 | def _call(prompt: str, system: str = None, max_tokens: int = 800) -> str:
 26 |     """
 27 |     Make a single LLM API call. Returns response text.
 28 |     Falls back gracefully if API key not set.
 29 |     """
 30 |     if not _available():
 31 |         return None
 32 | 
 33 |     try:
 34 |         if LLM_PROVIDER == "watsonx":
 35 |             return _call_watsonx(prompt, system, max_tokens)
 36 |         else:
 37 |             warn(f"Unknown LLM provider: {LLM_PROVIDER}")
 38 |             return None
 39 | 
 40 |     except Exception as e:
 41 |         warn(f"LLM call failed: {e} — falling back to deterministic output")
 42 |         return None
 43 |

 45 | def _call_watsonx(prompt: str, system: str = None, max_tokens: int = 800) -> str:
 46 |     """Make a call to IBM watsonx.ai."""
 47 |     from ibm_watsonx_ai.foundation_models import ModelInference
 48 |     from ibm_watsonx_ai.metanames import GenTextParamsMetaNames as GenParams
 49 |     
 50 |     # Combine system and user prompts
 51 |     full_prompt = prompt
 52 |     if system:
 53 |         full_prompt = f"{system}\n\n{prompt}"
 54 |     
 55 |     # Initialize model
 56 |     model = ModelInference(
 57 |         model_id=LLM_MODEL,
 58 |         api_key=WATSONX_API_KEY,
 59 |         project_id=WATSONX_PROJECT_ID,
 60 |         url=WATSONX_URL,
 61 |         params={
 62 |             GenParams.MAX_NEW_TOKENS: max_tokens,
 63 |             GenParams.TEMPERATURE: 0.2,
 64 |             GenParams.TOP_P: 1,
 65 |             GenParams.TOP_K: 50,
 66 |         }
 67 |     )
 68 |     
 69 |     # Generate response
 70 |     response = model.generate_text(prompt=full_prompt)
 71 |     return response.strip() if response else None
 72 | 
 73 | 
 74 | def _parse_json(text: str) -> dict | None:
 75 |     """Safely parse JSON from LLM response, stripping markdown fences."""
 76 |     if not text:
 77 |         return None
 78 |     try:
 79 |         clean = text.strip()
 80 |         if clean.startswith("```"):
 81 |             clean = clean.split("```")[1]
 82 |             if clean.startswith("json"):
 83 |                 clean = clean[4:]
 84 |         return json.loads(clean.strip())
 85 |     except Exception:
 86 |         return None
 87 | 
 88 | 
 89 | # ── CALL 1: PROBLEM INFERENCE ─────────────────────────────────
 90 | def infer_problem(profile: dict, heuristic_result: str) -> dict:
 91 |     """
 92 |     Used when heuristic confidence is low.
 93 |     Returns: {"problem_type": "regression"|"classification", "reason": str}
 94 |     """
 95 |     if not _available():
 96 |         return {"problem_type": heuristic_result, "reason": "LLM unavailable — used heuristic", "source": "heuristic"}
 97 | 
 98 |     info("Consulting LLM for problem type confirmation...")
 99 | 
100 |     # Build compact profile summary — keep tokens low
101 |     cols_summary = []
102 |     for col, info_dict in profile.get("columns", {}).items():
103 |         cols_summary.append({
104 |             "name": col,
105 |             "type": info_dict.get("type", info_dict.get("dtype")),
106 |             "nunique": info_dict.get("nunique"),
107 |             "is_target": info_dict.get("is_target", False),
108 |         })
109 | 
110 |     prompt = f"""Given this dataset profile, determine the ML problem type.
111 | 
112 | Dataset:
113 | - Rows: {profile['rows']}
114 | - Target column: {profile['target']}
115 | - Columns: {json.dumps(cols_summary, indent=2)}
116 | 
117 | Heuristic guess: {heuristic_result}
118 | 
119 | Respond ONLY with valid JSON, no explanation outside it:
120 | {{"problem_type": "regression" or "classification", "reason": "one sentence explanation"}}"""
121 | 
122 |     response = _call(prompt, max_tokens=150)
123 |     parsed = _parse_json(response)
124 | 
125 |     if parsed and "problem_type" in parsed:
126 |         parsed["source"] = "llm"
127 |         return parsed
128 | 
129 |     # Fallback
130 |     return {"problem_type": heuristic_result, "reason": "LLM response unclear — used heuristic", "source": "heuristic"}
131 | 
132 | 
133 | # ── CALL 2: RESULT INTERPRETATION ────────────────────────────
134 | def interpret_results(metrics: dict, problem_type: str, model_label: str,
135 |                       confidence: str, confidence_reasons: list,
136 |                       feature_names: list, profile: dict) -> str:
137 |     """
138 |     Generate a plain-English interpretation of training results.
139 |     Returns a 3-5 sentence summary string.
140 |     """
141 |     if not _available():
142 |         return _fallback_interpretation(metrics, problem_type, model_label, confidence)
143 | 
144 |     info("Generating result interpretation...")
145 | 
146 |     prompt = f"""You are a data scientist explaining ML results to a developer who is not an ML expert.
147 | 
148 | Model trained: {model_label}
149 | Problem type: {problem_type}
150 | Metrics: {json.dumps(metrics)}
151 | Confidence level: {confidence}
152 | Confidence reasons: {confidence_reasons}
153 | Features used: {feature_names}
154 | Dataset rows: {profile.get('rows', 'unknown')}
155 | 
156 | Write a plain-English interpretation in exactly 3-5 sentences. Cover:
157 | 1. How well the model performed and what that means practically
158 | 2. The most important thing to know about these results
159 | 3. One actionable suggestion to improve if confidence is Medium or Low
160 | 
161 | Do NOT use bullet points. Write in flowing sentences. No jargon."""
162 | 
163 |     response = _call(prompt, max_tokens=300)
164 | 
165 |     if response:
166 |         return response
167 | 
168 |     return _fallback_interpretation(metrics, problem_type, model_label, confidence)
169 |

171 | def _fallback_interpretation(metrics, problem_type, model_label, confidence) -> str:
172 |     if problem_type == "classification":
173 |         acc = metrics.get("Accuracy", "unknown")
174 |         return (
175 |             f"The {model_label} achieved an accuracy of {acc}. "
176 |             f"Confidence is {confidence} — check the report for details on what may be limiting performance. "
177 |             f"Review the generated train.py for the full pipeline and consider gathering more data if accuracy is low."
178 |         )
179 |     else:
180 |         r2 = metrics.get("R²", "unknown")
181 |         return (
182 |             f"The {model_label} achieved an R² of {r2}. "
183 |             f"Confidence is {confidence} — check the report for details. "
184 |             f"Review train.py for the full pipeline."
185 |         )
186 |

194 |     We don't ask LLM to write the whole file — just the explanatory comments.

def _call_watsonx(prompt: str, system: str = None, max_tokens: int = 800) -> str:
    """Make a call to IBM watsonx.ai."""
    from ibm_watsonx_ai.foundation_models import ModelInference
    from ibm_watsonx_ai.metanames import GenTextParamsMetaNames as GenParams
    
    # Combine system and user prompts
    full_prompt = prompt
    if system:
        full_prompt = f"{system}\n\n{prompt}"
    
    # Initialize model
    model = ModelInference(
        model_id=LLM_MODEL,
        api_key=WATSONX_API_KEY,
        project_id=WATSONX_PROJECT_ID,
        url=WATSONX_URL,
        params={
            GenParams.MAX_NEW_TOKENS: max_tokens,
            GenParams.TEMPERATURE: 0.2,
            GenParams.TOP_P: 1,
            GenParams.TOP_K: 50,
        }
    )

    response = model.generate_text(prompt=full_prompt)
    return response.strip() if response else None
=======
def _call_watsonx(prompt: str, system: str = None, max_tokens: int = 800) -> str:
    """Make a call to IBM watsonx.ai using proper SDK initialization."""
    from ibm_watsonx_ai import APIClient, Credentials
    from ibm_watsonx_ai.foundation_models import ModelInference
    
    # Combine system and user prompts
    full_prompt = prompt
    if system:
        full_prompt = f"{system}\n\n{prompt}"
    
    # Initialize credentials and client
    credentials = Credentials(
        url=WATSONX_URL,
        api_key=WATSONX_API_KEY
    )
    client = APIClient(credentials, project_id=WATSONX_PROJECT_ID)
    
    # Initialize model with client
    model = ModelInference(
        model_id=LLM_MODEL,
        api_client=client,
        params={
            "max_new_tokens": max_tokens,
            "temperature": 0.2,
            "top_p": 1,
            "top_k": 50,
        }
    )
    
    # Generate response
    response = model.generate_text(prompt=full_prompt)
    return response.strip() if response else None
>>>>>>> REPLACE
</diff>

**Assistant:**

Now let me work on **Task 5: Add train init Command**. First, I'll create the config.py file:

<write_to_file>
<path>traincli/config.py</path>
<content>
import os
from pathlib import Path
from rich.console import Console
from rich.prompt import Prompt

console = Console()


def get_config_path() -> Path:
    """Get the path to the global config file."""
    home = Path.home()
    config_dir = home / ".traincli"
    config_dir.mkdir(exist_ok=True)
    return config_dir / "config.env"


def init_config():
    """Interactive setup wizard for TrainCLI configuration."""
    console.print("\n[bold cyan]TrainCLI Setup[/bold cyan]")
    console.print("─" * 40)
    
    # Ask for LLM provider
    provider = Prompt.ask(
        "LLM Provider",
        choices=["watsonx", "groq", "none"],
        default="watsonx"
    )
    
    config_lines = [
        "# TrainCLI Configuration",
        "# Generated by: train init",
        "",
        f"LLM_PROVIDER={provider}",
    ]
    
    if provider == "watsonx":
        api_key = Prompt.ask("WatsonX API Key", password=True)
        project_id = Prompt.ask("WatsonX Project ID")
        url = Prompt.ask(
            "WatsonX URL",
            default="https://us-south.ml.cloud.ibm.com"
        )
        
        config_lines.extend([
            f"WATSONX_API_KEY={api_key}",
            f"WATSONX_PROJECT_ID={project_id}",
            f"WATSONX_URL={url}",
            "LLM_MODEL=ibm/granite-13b-instruct-v2",
        ])
    
    elif provider == "groq":
        api_key = Prompt.ask("Groq API Key", password=True)
        config_lines.extend([
            f"GROQ_API_KEY={api_key}",
            "LLM_MODEL=llama-3.1-70b-versatile",
        ])
    
    else:
        config_lines.append("# No LLM provider configured — offline mode")
    
    # Write config
    config_path = get_config_path()
    with open(config_path, "w") as f:
        f.write("\n".join(config_lines))
    
    console.print(f"\n[green]✓[/green] Config saved to [cyan]{config_path}[/cyan]")
    console.print("[green]✓[/green] Run: [bold]train --data ./data.csv --target column[/bold]\n")


def load_config():
    """Load configuration from global config file if it exists."""
    config_path = get_config_path()
    if config_path.exists():
        from dotenv import load_dotenv
        load_dotenv(config_path)
</content>
<line_count>72</line_count>
</write_to_file>

<content>
# TrainCLI

**Train ML models from a single command — no code required.**

TrainCLI is a command-line tool that automates the entire machine learning pipeline: data profiling, cleaning, model selection, training, and export. Perfect for rapid prototyping, baseline models, or learning ML workflows.

## Features

- 🚀 **One-command training** — `train --data data.csv --target column`
- 🤖 **Auto model selection** — Cross-validation picks the best algorithm
- 🧹 **Smart data cleaning** — Handles missing values, outliers, encoding
- 📊 **Data profiling** — Detects issues before training
- 🔍 **Leakage detection** — Warns about suspiciously correlated features
- 🧠 **LLM-powered insights** — Optional AI explanations (watsonx.ai)
- 📦 **Export everything** — model.pkl, train.py, report.md, metrics.json
- 🔧 **Reproducible** — Generated train.py is standalone

## Installation

```bash
pip install traincli
```

## Quick Start

### 1. Initialize (first time only)

```bash
train init
```

This sets up your API keys for LLM features (optional — works offline too).

### 2. Train a model

```bash
train --data sales.csv --target revenue
```

That's it! TrainCLI will:
- Profile your data
- Clean it automatically (or ask for input)
- Detect if it's classification or regression
- Try multiple models via cross-validation
- Pick the best one
- Export everything to `./output/`

### 3. Use your model

```python
import pickle
import pandas as pd

with open("output/model.pkl", "rb") as f:
    model = pickle.load(f)

new_data = pd.DataFrame([{"feature1": 10, "feature2": "A"}])
prediction = model.predict(new_data)
```

Or run the generated `train.py` to retrain from scratch.

## Commands

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `train --data <file> --target <col>` | Train a model on a CSV file |
| `train --dir <folder> --target <col>` | Train on all CSVs in a folder |
| `train --model <name>` | Use a specific model (e.g., `random_forest`) |
| `train --model ?` | Pick model interactively |
| `train --task classification` | Override problem type detection |
| `train --drop col1,col2` | Drop columns (e.g., to fix leakage) |
| `train --preview` | Profile data without training |
| `train --auto` | Skip all prompts (for CI/CD) |
| `train init` | Configure API keys |

## Examples

### Basic training
```bash
train --data customers.csv --target churn
```

### Force a specific model
```bash
train --data sales.csv --target price --model gradient_boosting
```

### Interactive model selection
```bash
train --data data.csv --target label --model ?
```

### Drop leaky columns
```bash
train --data jobs.csv --target salary --drop min_salary,max_salary
```

### Batch processing
```bash
train --dir ./datasets/ --target outcome --auto
```

### Preview mode
```bash
train --data data.csv --target col --preview
```

## Output Files

After training, you'll get:

- **model.pkl** — Trained scikit-learn pipeline (ready to use)
- **train.py** — Standalone script to retrain the model
- **report.md** — Human-readable summary with metrics
- **metrics.json** — Machine-readable metrics
- **session.json** — Full training session metadata

## Supported Models

TrainCLI includes:

**Classification:**
- Logistic Regression
- Random Forest
- Gradient Boosting (XGBoost)
- Support Vector Machine
- K-Nearest Neighbors

**Regression:**
- Linear Regression
- Ridge Regression
- Random Forest
- Gradient Boosting (XGBoost)
- Support Vector Regression

## LLM Features (Optional)

TrainCLI can use IBM watsonx.ai to:
- Explain model results in plain English
- Suggest improvements
- Generate educational comments in train.py

To enable:
```bash
train init
# Choose "watsonx" and enter your API key
```

Works offline if no API key is configured.

## Data Leakage Detection

TrainCLI automatically checks for:
- Features with >0.98 correlation to target
- Column names containing the target name
- Linear transformations of the target

Example warning:
```
⚠ Leakage suspected:
  → min_salary: correlation with target is 0.999 — suspiciously high
  
  Suggested fix: train --drop min_salary ...
```

## Requirements

- Python 3.9+
- pandas, scikit-learn, xgboost
- Optional: ibm-watsonx-ai (for LLM features)

## Development

```bash
git clone https://github.com/yourusername/traincli
cd traincli
pip install -e .
```

## License

MIT

## Contributing

Contributions welcome! Open an issue or PR.

## Roadmap

- [ ] Meta-model for smarter algorithm selection
- [ ] MCP server for Claude integration
- [ ] More preprocessing options
- [ ] Feature engineering suggestions
- [ ] Hyperparameter tuning

<write_to_file>
<path>traincli/core.py</path>
<content>
"""
Core pipeline logic — used by both CLI and MCP server.
"""
import pandas as pd
from pathlib import Path
from traincli.utils.session import Session
from traincli.profiler import profile
from traincli.cleaner import clean
from traincli.detector import detect
from traincli.trainer import train
from traincli.exporter import export


def run_pipeline(
    data_path: str,
    target: str,
    model_key: str = None,
    task: str = None,
    out: str = "./output",
    auto: bool = True,
    drop: str = None,
) -> dict:
    """
    Core ML pipeline — loads data, profiles, cleans, trains, exports.
    
    Args:
        data_path: Path to CSV file
        target: Target column name
        model_key: Model to use (None = auto-select)
        task: Problem type override ("classification" or "regression")
        out: Output directory
        auto: Skip interactive prompts
        drop: Comma-separated columns to drop
    
    Returns:
        dict with keys: results, df_clean, profile, output_dir
    """
    # Load
    path = Path(data_path)
    if not path.exists():
        raise FileNotFoundError(f"File not found: {data_path}")
    
    try:
        df = pd.read_csv(path)
    except Exception as e:
        raise ValueError(f"Could not read CSV: {e}")
    
    if target not in df.columns:
        raise ValueError(f"Target '{target}' not found. Available: {list(df.columns)}")
    
    session = Session(data_path, target)
    
    # Profile
    prof = profile(df, target)
    session.set_profile({
        "rows": prof["rows"],
        "cols": prof["cols"],
        "null_pct": prof["null_pct"],
        "issues_found": len(prof["issues"]),
    })
    
    # Drop columns if requested
    if drop:
        cols_to_drop = [c.strip() for c in drop.split(",")]
        cols_to_drop = [c for c in cols_to_drop if c in df.columns and c != target]
        if cols_to_drop:
            df = df.drop(columns=cols_to_drop)
    
    # Clean
    df_clean = clean(df, prof, session, auto=auto)
    
    # Detect problem type
    if task:
        session.set_problem(task, "user_flag")
        problem_type = task
    else:
        problem_type = detect(df_clean, target, session)
    
    # Train
    results = train(
        df=df_clean,
        target=target,
        problem_type=problem_type,
        session=session,
        model_key=model_key,
        interactive=not auto,
        profile=prof,
    )
    
    # Export
    output_dir = Path(out)
    export(results, df_clean, target, data_path, output_dir, session)
    
    return {
        "results": results,
        "df_clean": df_clean,
        "profile": prof,
        "output_dir": str(output_dir.resolve()),
        "session": session,
    }


def profile_dataset(data_path: str, target: str = None) -> dict:
    """
    Profile a dataset without training.
    
    Args:
        data_path: Path to CSV file
        target: Optional target column (for leakage detection)
    
    Returns:
        Profile dict with dataset statistics
    """
    path = Path(data_path)
    if not path.exists():
        raise FileNotFoundError(f"File not found: {data_path}")
    
    try:
        df = pd.read_csv(path)
    except Exception as e:
        raise ValueError(f"Could not read CSV: {e}")
    
    # If no target specified, use first column
    if not target:
        target = df.columns[0]
    
    if target not in df.columns:
        raise ValueError(f"Target '{target}' not found. Available: {list(df.columns)}")
    
    prof = profile(df, target)
    return prof


def suggest_target(data_path: str) -> dict:
    """
    Suggest the best target column for a dataset.
    
    Args:
        data_path: Path to CSV file
    
    Returns:
        dict with suggested target and reasoning
    """
    path = Path(data_path)
    if not path.exists():
        raise FileNotFoundError(f"File not found: {data_path}")
    
    try:
        df = pd.read_csv(path)
    except Exception as e:
        raise ValueError(f"Could not read CSV: {e}")
    
    # Heuristics for target selection:
    # 1. Column named "target", "label", "y", "outcome"
    # 2. Last column (common convention)
    # 3. Column with moderate cardinality (not ID, not free text)
    
    target_keywords = ["target", "label", "y", "outcome", "class", "prediction"]
    
    for col in df.columns:
        if col.lower() in target_keywords:
            return {
                "suggested_target": col,
                "reason": f"Column name '{col}' suggests it's the target",
                "confidence": "high"
            }
    
    # Check last column
    last_col = df.columns[-1]
    nunique = df[last_col].nunique()
    total = len(df)
    
    if 2 <= nunique <= total * 0.5:
        return {
            "suggested_target": last_col,
            "reason": f"Last column with {nunique} unique values (common convention)",
            "confidence": "medium"
        }
    
    # Fallback: find column with reasonable cardinality
    for col in df.columns:
        nunique = df[col].nunique()
        if 2 <= nunique <= total * 0.5:
            return {
                "suggested_target": col,
                "reason": f"Column has {nunique} unique values (suitable for prediction)",
                "confidence": "low"
            }
    
    return {
        "suggested_target": df.columns[-1],
        "reason": "No clear target found — defaulting to last column",
        "confidence": "very_low"
    }
</content>

<content>
"""
MCP Server for TrainCLI — enables Claude Code to train ML models.
"""
import asyncio
import json
from mcp.server import Server
from mcp.server.stdio import stdio_server
from mcp.types import Tool, TextContent

from traincli.core import run_pipeline, profile_dataset, suggest_target


# Initialize MCP server
app = Server("traincli")


@app.list_tools()
async def list_tools() -> list[Tool]:
    """List available tools."""
    return [
        Tool(
            name="train_model",
            description="Train a machine learning model on a CSV file. Automatically profiles data, cleans it, selects the best model via cross-validation, and exports everything.",
            inputSchema={
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "data": {
                        "type": "string",
                        "description": "Path to CSV file"
                    },
                    "target": {
                        "type": "string",
                        "description": "Target column name to predict"
                    },
                    "model": {
                        "type": "string",
                        "description": "Optional: specific model to use (e.g., 'random_forest', 'gradient_boosting'). If not provided, auto-selects via CV.",
                        "default": None
                    },
                    "task": {
                        "type": "string",
                        "enum": ["classification", "regression"],
                        "description": "Optional: override problem type detection",
                        "default": None
                    },
                    "drop": {
                        "type": "string",
                        "description": "Optional: comma-separated columns to drop (e.g., 'col1,col2')",
                        "default": None
                    },
                    "output": {
                        "type": "string",
                        "description": "Output directory path",
                        "default": "./output"
                    }
                },
                "required": ["data", "target"]
            }
        ),
        Tool(
            name="profile_dataset",
            description="Profile a CSV dataset to understand its structure, detect issues, and check for data leakage. Does not train a model.",
            inputSchema={
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "data": {
                        "type": "string",
                        "description": "Path to CSV file"
                    },
                    "target": {
                        "type": "string",
                        "description": "Optional: target column for leakage detection",
                        "default": None
                    }
                },
                "required": ["data"]
            }
        ),
        Tool(
            name="suggest_target",
            description="Suggest the best target column for a dataset based on heuristics (column names, cardinality, position).",
            inputSchema={
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "data": {
                        "type": "string",
                        "description": "Path to CSV file"
                    }
                },
                "required": ["data"]
            }
        )
    ]


@app.call_tool()
async def call_tool(name: str, arguments: dict) -> list[TextContent]:
    """Handle tool calls."""
    
    if name == "train_model":
        try:
            result = run_pipeline(
                data_path=arguments["data"],
                target=arguments["target"],
                model_key=arguments.get("model"),
                task=arguments.get("task"),
                out=arguments.get("output", "./output"),
                auto=True,
                drop=arguments.get("drop")
            )
            
            # Format response
            metrics = result["results"]["metrics"]
            model_label = result["results"]["model_entry"]["label"]
            confidence = result["results"]["confidence"]
            
            response = {
                "status": "success",
                "model": model_label,
                "metrics": metrics,
                "confidence": confidence,
                "output_directory": result["output_dir"],
                "files": [
                    "model.pkl",
                    "train.py",
                    "report.md",
                    "metrics.json",
                    "session.json"
                ],
                "interpretation": result["results"].get("interpretation", "")
            }
            
            return [TextContent(
                type="text",
                text=json.dumps(response, indent=2)
            )]
            
        except Exception as e:
            return [TextContent(
                type="text",
                text=json.dumps({
                    "status": "error",
                    "error": str(e)
                }, indent=2)
            )]
    
    elif name == "profile_dataset":
        try:
            prof = profile_dataset(
                data_path=arguments["data"],
                target=arguments.get("target")
            )
            
            # Simplify profile for response
            response = {
                "status": "success",
                "rows": prof["rows"],
                "cols": prof["cols"],
                "target": prof["target"],
                "null_percentage": prof["null_pct"],
                "issues_found": len(prof["issues"]),
                "issues": prof["issues"],
                "leakage_suspects": prof.get("leakage", []),
                "columns": {
                    col: {
                        "type": info.get("type", info.get("dtype")),
                        "null_pct": info.get("null_pct", 0),
                        "nunique": info.get("nunique", 0)
                    }
                    for col, info in prof["columns"].items()
                }
            }
            
            return [TextContent(
                type="text",
                text=json.dumps(response, indent=2)
            )]
            
        except Exception as e:
            return [TextContent(
                type="text",
                text=json.dumps({
                    "status": "error",
                    "error": str(e)
                }, indent=2)
            )]
    
    elif name == "suggest_target":
        try:
            suggestion = suggest_target(arguments["data"])
            
            return [TextContent(
                type="text",
                text=json.dumps({
                    "status": "success",
                    **suggestion
                }, indent=2)
            )]
            
        except Exception as e:
            return [TextContent(
                type="text",
                text=json.dumps({
                    "status": "error",
                    "error": str(e)
                }, indent=2)
            )]
    
    else:
        return [TextContent(
            type="text",
            text=json.dumps({
                "status": "error",
                "error": f"Unknown tool: {name}"
            }, indent=2)
        )]


async def main():
    """Run the MCP server."""
    async with stdio_server() as (read_stream, write_stream):
        await app.run(
            read_stream,
            write_stream,
            app.create_initialization_options()
        )


if __name__ == "__main__":
    asyncio.run(main())
</content>

## Roadmap

- [ ] Meta-model for smarter algorithm selection
- [ ] MCP server for Claude integration
- [ ] More preprocessing options
- [ ] Feature engineering suggestions
- [ ] Hyperparameter tuning

---

**Made with ❤️ for developers who want ML without the boilerplate.**
=======
## MCP Server (Claude Code Integration)

TrainCLI includes an MCP server that lets Claude Code train models directly:

### Setup

1. Install TrainCLI:
```bash
pip install traincli
```

2. Add to your Claude Desktop config (`~/Library/Application Support/Claude/claude_desktop_config.json` on Mac):
```json
{
  "mcpServers": {
    "traincli": {
      "command": "traincli-mcp"
    }
  }
}
```

3. Restart Claude Desktop

### Available Tools

- **train_model** — Train a model on a CSV file
- **profile_dataset** — Profile data without training
- **suggest_target** — Suggest the best target column

### Example Usage in Claude

```
User: Train a model on sales.csv to predict revenue

Claude: [calls train_model tool]
✓ Model trained: Gradient Boosting
✓ R² = 0.847
✓ Files saved to ./output/
```

## Roadmap

- [ ] Meta-model for smarter algorithm selection
- [ ] More preprocessing options
- [ ] Feature engineering suggestions
- [ ] Hyperparameter tuning

---

**Made with ❤️ for developers who want ML without the boilerplate.**

<write_to_file>
<path>traincli/meta_collector.py</path>
<content>
"""
Meta-model data collection — tracks which models work best for different dataset characteristics.
"""
import os
import json
import pandas as pd
from pathlib import Path
from datetime import datetime


def get_meta_dataset_path() -> Path:
    """Get path to the global meta-dataset CSV."""
    home = Path.home()
    config_dir = home / ".traincli"
    config_dir.mkdir(exist_ok=True)
    return config_dir / "meta_dataset.csv"


def collect_meta_features(df: pd.DataFrame, target: str, results: dict) -> dict:
    """
    Extract meta-features from a training run.
    
    Args:
        df: Cleaned dataframe (post-cleaning, pre-training)
        target: Target column name
        results: Training results dict
    
    Returns:
        dict of meta-features
    """
    X = df.drop(columns=[target])
    y = df[target]
    
    # Dataset characteristics
    rows = len(df)
    cols = len(X.columns)
    null_pct = (df.isnull().sum().sum() / (rows * cols)) * 100
    
    # Feature type ratios
    numeric_cols = X.select_dtypes(include=['number']).columns
    categorical_cols = X.select_dtypes(include=['object', 'category']).columns
    numeric_ratio = len(numeric_cols) / cols if cols > 0 else 0
    categorical_ratio = len(categorical_cols) / cols if cols > 0 else 0
    
    # Target characteristics
    target_nunique = y.nunique()
    target_is_float = pd.api.types.is_float_dtype(y)
    
    # Target range (for regression) or class balance (for classification)
    if results["problem_type"] == "regression":
        target_range = float(y.max() - y.min()) if len(y) > 0 else 0
        target_balance = None
    else:
        target_range = None
        # Class balance: ratio of smallest to largest class
        value_counts = y.value_counts()
        if len(value_counts) > 1:
            target_balance = float(value_counts.min() / value_counts.max())
        else:
            target_balance = 1.0
    
    # Best model from CV
    best_model = results["model_entry"]["key"]
    best_cv_score = float(results["cv_scores"].mean())
    
    meta_features = {
        "timestamp": datetime.now().isoformat(),
        "rows": rows,
        "cols": cols,
        "null_pct": round(null_pct, 2),
        "numeric_ratio": round(numeric_ratio, 2),
        "categorical_ratio": round(categorical_ratio, 2),
        "target_nunique": target_nunique,
        "target_is_float": int(target_is_float),
        "target_range": target_range,
        "target_balance": target_balance,
        "problem_type": results["problem_type"],
        "best_model": best_model,
        "best_cv_score": round(best_cv_score, 4),
    }
    
    return meta_features


def append_to_meta_dataset(meta_features: dict):
    """
    Append a training run's meta-features to the global meta-dataset.
    
    Args:
        meta_features: dict from collect_meta_features()
    """
    meta_path = get_meta_dataset_path()
    
    # Convert to DataFrame row
    row_df = pd.DataFrame([meta_features])
    
    # Append or create
    if meta_path.exists():
        existing = pd.read_csv(meta_path)
        combined = pd.concat([existing, row_df], ignore_index=True)
        combined.to_csv(meta_path, index=False)
    else:
        row_df.to_csv(meta_path, index=False)


def get_meta_dataset_stats() -> dict:
    """Get statistics about the collected meta-dataset."""
    meta_path = get_meta_dataset_path()
    
    if not meta_path.exists():
        return {
            "exists": False,
            "rows": 0,
            "message": "No meta-dataset yet. Run with --meta flag to start collecting."
        }
    
    df = pd.read_csv(meta_path)
    
    # Count by model
    model_counts = df["best_model"].value_counts().to_dict()
    
    return {
        "exists": True,
        "rows": len(df),
        "path": str(meta_path),
        "model_distribution": model_counts,
        "problem_types": df["problem_type"].value_counts().to_dict(),
        "avg_cv_score": round(df["best_cv_score"].mean(), 4),
    }
</content>

Now let me create a script to fetch sklearn datasets for meta-model training:

<write_to_file>
<path>scripts/fetch_sklearn_datasets.py</path>
<content>
"""
Fetch sklearn built-in datasets and run TrainCLI on them with --meta flag.
This builds the initial meta-dataset for meta-model training.
"""
import os
import sys
from pathlib import Path
import pandas as pd
from sklearn import datasets

# Add parent directory to path
sys.path.insert(0, str(Path(__file__).parent.parent))

from traincli.core import run_pipeline
from traincli.meta_collector import collect_meta_features, append_to_meta_dataset


def fetch_and_train():
    """Fetch sklearn datasets and train models on them."""
    
    output_dir = Path("./sklearn_datasets")
    output_dir.mkdir(exist_ok=True)
    
    datasets_to_fetch = [
        {
            "name": "iris",
            "loader": datasets.load_iris,
            "target": "target",
            "task": "classification"
        },
        {
            "name": "wine",
            "loader": datasets.load_wine,
            "target": "target",
            "task": "classification"
        },
        {
            "name": "breast_cancer",
            "loader": datasets.load_breast_cancer,
            "target": "target",
            "task": "classification"
        },
        {
            "name": "diabetes",
            "loader": datasets.load_diabetes,
            "target": "target",
            "task": "regression"
        },
        {
            "name": "digits",
            "loader": datasets.load_digits,
            "target": "target",
            "task": "classification"
        },
    ]
    
    print("Fetching sklearn datasets and training models...")
    print("=" * 60)
    
    for ds_info in datasets_to_fetch:
        print(f"\n📊 Processing: {ds_info['name']}")
        
        # Load dataset
        data = ds_info["loader"]()
        df = pd.DataFrame(data.data, columns=data.feature_names if hasattr(data, 'feature_names') else [f"feature_{i}" for i in range(data.data.shape[1])])
        df[ds_info["target"]] = data.target
        
        # Save to CSV
        csv_path = output_dir / f"{ds_info['name']}.csv"
        df.to_csv(csv_path, index=False)
        print(f"  ✓ Saved to {csv_path}")
        
        # Train with TrainCLI
        try:
            result = run_pipeline(
                data_path=str(csv_path),
                target=ds_info["target"],
                task=ds_info["task"],
                out=str(output_dir / ds_info["name"] / "output"),
                auto=True
            )
            
            # Collect meta-features
            meta_features = collect_meta_features(
                result["df_clean"],
                ds_info["target"],
                result["results"]
            )
            append_to_meta_dataset(meta_features)
            
            print(f"  ✓ Trained: {result['results']['model_entry']['label']}")
            print(f"  ✓ CV Score: {result['results']['cv_scores'].mean():.4f}")
            print(f"  ✓ Meta-features collected")
            
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"  ✗ Error: {e}")
    
    print("\n" + "=" * 60)
    print("✓ Done! Meta-dataset updated.")
    
    # Show stats
    from traincli.meta_collector import get_meta_dataset_stats
    stats = get_meta_dataset_stats()
    print(f"\nMeta-dataset stats:")
    print(f"  Total runs: {stats['rows']}")
    print(f"  Models: {stats.get('model_distribution', {})}")


if __name__ == "__main__":
    fetch_and_train()
</content>

 52 | def train(
 53 |     df: pd.DataFrame,
 54 |     target: str,
 55 |     problem_type: str,
 56 |     session: Session,
 57 |     model_key: str = None,
 58 |     interactive: bool = True,
 59 |     profile: dict = None,
 60 | ) -> dict:
 61 |     """
 62 |     Build pipeline, train model, evaluate, return results dict.
 63 |     """
 64 |     from rich.console import Console
 65 |     console = Console()
 66 | 
 67 |     header("Training")
 68 | 
 69 |     # ── FEATURES & TARGET ────────────────────────────────────
 70 |     X = df.drop(columns=[target])
 71 |     y = df[target].copy()
 72 | 
 73 |     # Encode categorical features
 74 |     label_encoders = {}
 75 |     for col in X.select_dtypes(include="object").columns:
 76 |         le = LabelEncoder()
 77 |         X[col] = le.fit_transform(X[col].astype(str))
 78 |         label_encoders[col] = le
 79 | 
 80 |     # Encode target if classification and object dtype
 81 |     target_encoder = None
 82 |     if problem_type == "classification" and y.dtype == object:
 83 |         le = LabelEncoder()
 84 |         y = pd.Series(le.fit_transform(y), name=target)
 85 |         target_encoder = le
 86 | 
 87 |     # ── MODEL SELECTION ──────────────────────────────────────
 88 |     model_entry = None
 89 | 
 90 |     if model_key == "?":
 91 |         if not interactive:
 92 |             model_entry = get_default(problem_type)
 93 |             session.set_model(model_entry["key"], model_entry["label"], "auto_default")
 94 |         else:
 95 |             model_entry = select_model_interactive(problem_type)
 96 |             session.set_model(model_entry["key"], model_entry["label"], "user_interactive")
 97 | 
 98 |     elif model_key is not None:
 99 |         model_entry = get_model(problem_type, model_key)
100 | 
101 |         if model_entry is None:
102 |             # Check wrong problem type
103 |             other = "classification" if problem_type == "regression" else "regression"
104 |             wrong_entry = get_model(other, model_key)
105 |             if wrong_entry:
106 |                 warn(f"'{model_key}' is a {other} model but your problem is {problem_type}.")
107 |                 if interactive:
108 |                     import click
109 |                     proceed = click.confirm("  Proceed anyway?", default=False)
110 |                     if not proceed:
111 |                         model_entry = get_default(problem_type)
112 |                         warn(f"Using recommended: {model_entry['label']}")
113 |                     else:
114 |                         model_entry = wrong_entry
115 |                 else:
116 |                     model_entry = get_default(problem_type)
117 |             else:
118 |                 warn(f"Unknown model '{model_key}' — using recommended default")
119 |                 model_entry = get_default(problem_type)
120 | 
121 |         session.set_model(model_entry["key"], model_entry["label"], "user_flag")
122 | 
123 |     else:
124 |         info("No model specified — running candidates and picking best...")
125 |         model_entry = _auto_select(X, y, problem_type, session)
126 | 
127 |     info(f"Model: [bold]{model_entry['label']}[/bold]")
128 | 
129 |     # ── PIPELINE ─────────────────────────────────────────────
130 |     pipeline = Pipeline([
131 |         ("imputer", SimpleImputer(strategy="median")),
132 |         ("scaler", StandardScaler()),
133 |         ("model", model_entry["class"](**model_entry["params"])),
134 |     ])
135 |

137 |     try:
138 |         stratify = y if problem_type == "classification" else None

140 |             X, y, test_size=0.2, random_state=42, stratify=stratify
141 |         )

145 |             X, y, test_size=0.2, random_state=42
146 |         )

225 | def improve(model_path: str, new_data_path: str, target: str, session: Session) -> dict:
226 |     """
227 |     Load an existing model, retrain on new data, compare metrics.
228 |     """
229 |     header("Improve mode")
230 | 
231 |     # Load existing model
232 |     path = Path(model_path)
233 |     if not path.exists():
234 |         raise FileNotFoundError(f"Model not found: {model_path}")
235 | 
236 |     with open(path, "rb") as f:
237 |         old_pipeline = pickle.load(f)
238 | 
239 |     info(f"Loaded existing model from {model_path}")
240 | 
241 |     # Load new data
242 |     df_new = pd.read_csv(new_data_path)
243 |     if target not in df_new.columns:
244 |         raise ValueError(f"Target '{target}' not found in new data")
245 | 
246 |     info(f"New data: {len(df_new):,} rows")
247 | 
248 |     X_new = df_new.drop(columns=[target])
249 |     y_new = df_new[target]
250 | 
251 |     # Encode categoricals
252 |     for col in X_new.select_dtypes(include="object").columns:
253 |         le = LabelEncoder()
254 |         X_new[col] = le.fit_transform(X_new[col].astype(str))
255 | 
256 |     if y_new.dtype == object:
257 |         le = LabelEncoder()
258 |         y_new = pd.Series(le.fit_transform(y_new))
259 | 
260 |     X_train, X_test, y_train, y_test = train_test_split(
261 |         X_new, y_new, test_size=0.2, random_state=42
262 |     )
263 | 
264 |     # Score old model on new data
265 |     try:
266 |         old_score = old_pipeline.score(X_test, y_test)
267 |         info(f"Old model score on new data: {old_score:.4f}")
268 |     except Exception:
269 |         old_score = None
270 |         warn("Could not score old model on new data — feature mismatch likely")
271 | 
272 |     # Retrain
273 |     info("Retraining on new data...")
274 |     old_pipeline.fit(X_train, y_train)
275 |     new_score = old_pipeline.score(X_test, y_test)
276 |     info(f"New model score after retraining: {new_score:.4f}")
277 | 
278 |     if old_score is not None:
279 |         delta = new_score - old_score
280 |         color = "green" if delta >= 0 else "red"

307 |             continue
308 |         pipeline = Pipeline([

311 |             ("model", entry["class"](**entry["params"])),

316 |             info(f"  {entry['label']}: CV={mean:.3f}")

332 |     reasons = []

334 |

def _auto_select(X, y, problem_type: str, session: Session) -> dict:
    """Run top 2 candidates, return the one with best CV score."""
    
    # Try meta-model prediction first

        info(f"Meta-model recommends: [bold]{meta_recommendation}[/bold]")

    session.set_model(best_entry["key"], best_entry["label"], "auto_cv")
    
    # Check if meta-model agreed
    if meta_recommendation and best_entry["key"] == meta_recommendation:
        success(f"Selected: {best_entry['label']} (CV={best_score:.3f}) ✓ Meta-model confirmed")
    elif meta_recommendation:
        success(f"Selected: {best_entry['label']} (CV={best_score:.3f}) — Meta-model suggested {meta_recommendation} but CV disagreed")
    else:
        success(f"Selected: {best_entry['label']} (CV={best_score:.3f})")
    
    return best_entry


def _meta_predict(X, y, problem_type: str) -> str | None:
    """
    Use meta-model to predict best algorithm for this dataset.
    Returns model key or None if meta-model unavailable.
    """
    try:
        from traincli.meta_collector import get_meta_dataset_path
        import pickle
        
        # Check if meta-model exists
        meta_model_path = Path(__file__).parent / "meta_model.pkl"
        if not meta_model_path.exists():
            return None
        
        # Check if we have enough meta-data
        meta_data_path = get_meta_dataset_path()
        if not meta_data_path.exists():
            return None
        
        meta_df = pd.read_csv(meta_data_path)
        if len(meta_df) < 10:  # Need at least 10 examples
            return None
        
        # Load meta-model
        with open(meta_model_path, "rb") as f:
            meta_model = pickle.load(f)
        
        # Extract meta-features from current dataset
        rows = len(X)
        cols = len(X.columns)
        numeric_cols = X.select_dtypes(include=['number']).columns
        categorical_cols = X.select_dtypes(include=['object', 'category']).columns
        numeric_ratio = len(numeric_cols) / cols if cols > 0 else 0
        categorical_ratio = len(categorical_cols) / cols if cols > 0 else 0
        
        target_nunique = y.nunique()
        target_is_float = int(pd.api.types.is_float_dtype(y))
        
        if problem_type == "regression":
            target_range = float(y.max() - y.min()) if len(y) > 0 else 0
            target_balance = None
        else:
            target_range = None
            value_counts = y.value_counts()
            if len(value_counts) > 1:
                target_balance = float(value_counts.min() / value_counts.max())
            else:
                target_balance = 1.0
        
        # Create feature vector
        features = pd.DataFrame([{
            "rows": rows,
            "cols": cols,
            "null_pct": 0,  # Already cleaned
            "numeric_ratio": numeric_ratio,
            "categorical_ratio": categorical_ratio,
            "target_nunique": target_nunique,
            "target_is_float": target_is_float,
            "target_range": target_range,
            "target_balance": target_balance,
        }])
        
        # Predict
        prediction = meta_model.predict(features)[0]
        return prediction
        
    except Exception:
        return None

<result>
🎉 **All 7 tasks completed successfully!** Projected score: **18/20** (+8.5 points)

## Summary of Changes

### ✅ Task 1: Fix Watsonx Integration (+1.5)
- Updated `llm.py` to use proper IBM watsonx.ai SDK with `APIClient` and `Credentials`
- Changed model to `ibm/granite-13b-instruct-v2`
- Created `.env.example` with proper configuration template
- Added global config loading from `~/.traincli/config.env`

### ✅ Task 2: Fix Data Leakage Detection (+1.0)
- Added `detect_leakage()` function in `profiler.py` with 3 checks:
  - Correlation > 0.98 with target
  - Column name contains target name
  - Linear transformation detection
- Added `--drop` flag to CLI for removing leaky columns
- Displays warnings with suggested fix command

### ✅ Task 3: Build Meta-model (+2.0)
- Created `meta_collector.py` for tracking dataset characteristics and best models
- Added `--meta` flag to collect training metadata
- Created `scripts/fetch_sklearn_datasets.py` to build initial meta-dataset
- Added `_meta_predict()` in `trainer.py` to use meta-model for algorithm recommendations
- Meta-model confirms or disagrees with CV results

### ✅ Task 4: Build MCP Server (+2.5)
- Created `core.py` with refactored pipeline logic (used by both CLI and MCP)
- Created `mcp_server.py` with 3 tools:
  - `train_model` — Train ML models
  - `profile_dataset` — Profile data without training
  - `suggest_target` — Suggest best target column
- Added `traincli-mcp` entry point to `pyproject.toml`
